It may be a problem if you have super sensitive skin, but I have a skin which is a little sensitive and I did not notice any adverse effects from using it.     <li> Why did no one tell me about electric shaving before?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Whomever came up with the idea that women need to shave half their bodies to go outside was probably a) a razor advertiser, and b) a man. It&#x27;s far less than with shaving though and doesn&#x27;t bother me, but if you&#x27;re looking for completely burn free shaving the super high end men&#x27;s razors might offer that experience.&lt;br /&gt;__________&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update:&lt;br /&gt;This shaver is all I wrote before, *when fully charged*.  If the battery is getting low, it starts yanking on your hairs, taking forever to get anything done, and just overall not working.  I would like to see Panasonic come out with a new model of this product with better battery technology.  The product literally does not function as it should without a close to full charge, which should not be the case.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There should also be a battery meter so you know when to recharge instead of having it die while you&#x27;re trying to shave and rush out the door.  I am tempted to buy a second one, so I can have one charging and one to use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;_________________&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update:&lt;br /&gt;I finally upgraded to a men&#x27;s 15000rpm Panasonic shaver.  The difference between that and this women&#x27;s shaver is a Mercedes Benz versus a garbage truck.  They will both get you there, but one is going to be a lot quieter, faster, and more comfortable.  Given that women shave more of their bodies than men it surprises me that there aren&#x27;t better shaving options for women.  I recommend getting a men&#x27;s shaver if you want the full experience.  I paid about 4-5x the cost of this shaver, but it is well worth it.  The women&#x27;s shaver had stopped working very well since it couldn&#x27;t get fully charged long enough to do both legs, frequently leaving me with only one leg shaved.  My new men&#x27;s shaver has a longer lasting battery with a battery meter and is &amp;#34;Made in Japan&amp;#34; versus &amp;#34;Made in China&amp;#34; for the women&#x27;s shaver.  The head is larger and pivots more.  It is an ugly black color, but other than that it is better on every level than this women&#x27;s shaver which now feels like a poorly functioning toy in comparison.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update: I didn&#x27;t want to recommend any particular men&#x27;s model, just that you buy a men&#x27;s electric razor instead, but due to popular demand, here is the model of men&#x27;s shaver I purchased: [[ASIN:B002N5MHLK Panasonic ES-LA93-K, Arc4 Electric Razor, Men&#x27;s 4-Blade with Multi-Flex Pivoting Head and Dual Motor, Premium Automatic Clean &amp; Charge Station Included, Wet or Dry Operation]] and my review of it: http://smile.amazon.com/review/R1BB4BSB822648/ref&#x3D;cm_cr_rdp_perm&lt;br /&gt;This was the highest end model available at the time and has been working very well for over 5 years.  But any men&#x27;s model should be fine, they appear to all be engineered to a higher standard than the women&#x27;s model - it&#x27;s not necessary to buy the top of the line, and I found the charging station superfluous after a year or so.&lt;br /&gt;____________________________________&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Further update:&lt;br /&gt;Another life changing upgrade!&lt;br /&gt;The men&#x27;s razor was still great, but shaving was taking too long, especially for longer hairs and large areas.  So after a lot of research and a long hesitation to spend more again on shaving equipment, I purchased an Oster cordless hair trimmer (for dogs) and an Andis Outliner blade  [[ASIN:B000MC7SQA Andis Outliner Beard Trimmer UltraEdge Detachable Blade, Silver, Size 1/150 (64160)]] to trim longer hairs and shave legs.  By reading reviews, I found out a lot of men use a hair trimmer on their face, as it is much gentler, and also works much better on longer hairs, but no one ever mentioned this for women!  It is at least 10x faster to shave and does not damage my (thin, pale, sensitive) skin. I also found out hair trimmers are used for surgery prep instead of razors to prevent small cuts in the skin.  It does leave a tiny bit of very short stubble, but I can leave the house with the result.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer works especially well before the electric shaver for a smooth result quickly without skin irritation.  I only wish I had found this sooner - I almost enjoy shaving now, and it can be done quickly, dry, anytime, with no injury.  Ignore any labels that say they are to trim dog&#x27;s hair, sheep, horses, men&#x27;s head hair, etc.  Hair is hair and trimming is trimming.  As a bonus you could also trim your dog, sheep, horses, and male relatives hair  (with a different blade).ith a battery meter and is &amp;#34;Made in Japan&amp;#34; versus &amp;#34;Made in China&amp;#34; for the women&#x27;s shaver.     <li> Although my wife was very happy with the results when shaving, this product has a design flaw. My wife is now on her second razor of this model and it has stopped working. The first was ordered Feb 14 2013 and the second Nov 14 2014. Both are still in warranty which right now is worthless as you will see later in this review. I am very knowledgeable about what makes things run and why they do not. When the razor is put into the charger one of the pins is pushed into the razor slightly to open a switch that prevents the razor from running while charging. This is a wonderful safety idea that prevents the charger from over heating. Only problem is that the switch design is very poor. When I opened the first razor and examined the switch I found that although it appeared to be closed it was not making an electrical connection. It was dirty, possibly from melted sealant or lubricant used. In either case simply touching the metal contacts allowed the razor head, which was still attached and in my hand to run. Actuating the switch by pushing and releasing the pin in the base of the battery housing caused the razor head to stop and it would not run until I pushed slightly on the contacts again. After reading other reviews where intermittent operation was mentioned or where premature battery failure occurred I can only conclude it was caused by this switch. I have called Panasonic and apparently their phones are not working properly and they can&#x27;t hear me after I have been switched to several departments. Although you must enter your phone number before you can be connected to anyone I never receive a call from them to find out why they can&#x27;t hear me. My wife now has 2 dead razors and I must take them apart to remove 2 good batteries for proper disposal.</li>

They wouldn&#x27;t cut one single hair and it&#x27;s not like I have crazy hair growth or anything.  My Husband is a knife collector/user and will sit an sharpen his knives while we watch movies and stuff, so I asked him about it.  He asked me if the shaver came with oil to treat it the blades.  No, it doesn&#x27;t.  He was like, if you get metal wet and then let it air dry, it will dull the edge of the blade.  That makes sense.  So, I bought the blade replacement set for it and he let&#x27;s me use his gun oil on the blade when I&#x27;m done and it&#x27;s been amazing ever since... who would have known!  It doesn&#x27;t say anything about oiling the blades in the instruction manual... guess they want to make that money on the replacement blades.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, after you use it... rinse the blades off, like take the part off and rinse it out... dry it with a towel real quick, then put it back together.  Put a dot of oil on each of the outer foils and on the two clippers on each end, then turn it on and run it for like 3 seconds.  That&#x27;s it.  I promise you, your shaver will now last way longer... thank sweet baby Jesus for guys that know about knives and stuff..
